Japanese troops have occupied the entire Four-Tao Railway, disarming the railway protection troops and police, and engaging in widespread looting and burning in Siping Street. Tongliao County was reported to have fallen again yesterday. The commander of the Japanese Kwantung Army in Shenyang issued an announcement stating that Japanese troops will permanently occupy Shenyang and calling on merchants to open their businesses immediately.

According to Tokyo dispatches, the Japanese government has decided to halt the advance on Harbin. The Foreign Ministry lodged its third serious protest with Japan yesterday, still demanding the immediate withdrawal of Japanese troops and the complete return of occupied territories. The Foreign Ministry received an urgent notification from the League of Nations Administrative Council, requesting both China and Japan to avoid any actions that could escalate the incident.

Tongliao City Fell Yesterday 2

(Tianjin) Tongliao dispatch: More than 300 Japanese troops in two armored trains arrived and occupied the county seat and railway station on the morning of the 23rd. (23rd Special Dispatch)

Japanese Second Division

Occupies Entire Four-Tao Line 3

Railway Protection Troops and Police Disarmed

(Beiping) Lieutenant General Tamon, commander of the Japanese Second Division, acting on the orders of Honjo, urgently departed for the Four-Tao Railway yesterday and has occupied the entire line. Railway police and railway protection troops have been disarmed. The Four-Tao Railway Bureau has been converted into the headquarters of the Japanese Second Division. The number of Japanese troops in the Siping Street area has increased to more than 1,500, engaged in looting, arson, and murder. (23rd Special Dispatch)

(Harbin) The South Manchuria Railway dispatched 130 line workers to be assigned to the Four-Tao and Jichang Railways. (22nd Special Dispatch)

(Tianjin) The entire Four-Tao Railway was occupied by Japanese troops on the 23rd, with Japanese flags hung at each station. (23rd Special Dispatch)

Japanese Troops Reach Juliuhe 4

(Tianjin) Urgent telegram from Huanggu Tun: At 5 p.m. on the 23rd, two Japanese armored trains, fully loaded with armed soldiers, forcibly passed through Huanggu Tun on the South Manchuria Railway and arrived at Juliuhe. (23rd Special Dispatch)

(Tianjin) Zhu Hua, the Huanggu Tun section chief, arrived in Tianjin on the evening of the 23rd and stated that the arrival of Japanese troops at Juliuhe was authorized in advance by the signature of Adviser Adachi of the Railway Bureau. (23rd Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) The Japanese garrison in Korea has been ordered to depart, with one unit heading to Juliuhe and another to Tongliao. (23rd Special Dispatch)

Japanese Announcement to Shenyang Residents

Permanent Occupation of Shenyang 5

Orders Merchants to Open Immediately

(Beiping) Japanese aircraft scattered announcements in Shenyang stating that the Japanese Imperial Army will permanently occupy Fengtian, hoping that the Chinese people will live in peace and work and will not obstruct the actions of the Imperial Army, causing inconvenience, etc. Furthermore, the announcement ordered merchants to open their businesses on the 23rd, and following the Dalian method, collect business taxes, and all Chinese taxes will be waived. The Japanese are reorganizing various Shenyang agencies, transferring personnel from the South Manchuria Railway to serve. As for the name of Fengtian, some are advocating changing it to Shengjing, while others are advocating merging it into the Kwantung Leased Territory. (23rd Special Dispatch)

(Harbin) The Japanese-appointed mayor of Fengtian has established five departments: general affairs, sanitation, finance, and civil engineering. (22nd Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) Li Dexin, the county magistrate of Shenyang, escaped from Shenyang in disguise and arrived in Beiping this afternoon, immediately reporting to the authorities. (23rd Special Dispatch)

(Harbin) Twelve Japanese aircraft from Pyongyang arrived in Liaoning. (22nd Special Dispatch)

(Tianjin) Telegram from Huanggu Tun: Honjo Shigeru, commander of the Kwantung Army, issued an announcement on the 22nd stating: (1) Because the Chinese troops in Fengtian are entirely lacking in popular support and causing disturbances, the Imperial Army will permanently occupy it. We hope that the Chinese people will live in peace and work and not obstruct us, causing inconvenience. (2) The Imperial Army will maintain stability in Fengtian. All shops should open for business, and from the 23rd, Chinese taxes will be abolished, and business taxes will be collected according to the Dalian method. (23rd Special Dispatch)

(Tianjin) Telegram from Huanggu Tun: The Japanese have transferred a large number of South Manchuria Railway personnel and have begun to reorganize various Shenyang agencies, also planning to rename it Shengjing. Another group of Japanese are advocating merging it into the Kwantung Leased Territory, so no decision has been made yet. (23rd Special Dispatch)

(Tianjin) Rumors that Zhang Zongchang is the commander-in-chief of the Kwantung Army's Chinese forces are completely untrue. (23rd Special Dispatch)

Japanese Troops Force

Xinmin Business Community to Raise Flags 6

(Beiping) After occupying Xinmin Tun, Japanese troops forced all merchants and residents to raise Japanese flags and prohibited them from closing their businesses. (23rd Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) Japanese aircraft dropped bombs on Xinmin Tun today. (23rd Special Dispatch)

Japanese Government Decides

Not to Send Troops to Harbin 7

(Tokyo) The acting Japanese Consul-General in Harbin, Nakagawa, telegraphed Foreign Minister Shidehara yesterday, stating that the situation in Harbin is urgent and requesting the dispatch of troops to protect Japanese residents. As a result of yesterday's cabinet meeting, it was decided not to dispatch troops to avoid escalating the incident. However, residents were ordered to temporarily evacuate to safe areas. The same policy will be applied to residents in other areas where no Japanese troops are deployed. Instructions have been issued to diplomats stationed abroad. (23rd Den-tsu News Agency Dispatch)

Beining Railway Requests

Japanese Side Remove Landmines 8

(Tianjin) The Beining Railway Bureau dispatched Adviser Adachi to Liaoning to negotiate with the Japanese consul, requesting the removal of landmines to facilitate the repair of tracks and maintain traffic. There has been no result yet. (23rd Special Dispatch)

(Tianjin) The Railway Bureau reports that Adachi telegraphed that the Japanese consul has agreed to allow Beining Railway trains to travel from Huanggu Tun to the Japanese station, with the Japanese army temporarily responsible for protection, but has not yet agreed to allow travel to Shenyang Station. (23rd Special Dispatch)

Foreign Ministry Received

League of Nations Emergency Notification 9

Telegram from Chairman Le Loux of the Executive Yuan States

Definite Measures for Immediate Troop Withdrawal

Are Being Negotiated and Implemented with Various Representatives

(Nanjing) The Foreign Ministry has just received a telegram from Le Loux, Chairman of the Executive Yuan of the League of Nations in Geneva, stating that regarding the incident in the three eastern provinces of China, the Chinese government requested assistance under Article 11 of the League of Nations Covenant. A meeting was specially convened today, and the Executive Yuan unanimously passed a resolution authorizing me to take the following actions: (1) Issue an urgent notification to the governments of China and Japan, urging them to avoid any actions that could escalate the incident or impede a peaceful resolution; (2) Negotiate with representatives of China and Japan a definite method to ensure that both countries immediately withdraw their troops and that the lives and property of the people of both countries are not harmed; (3) The Executive Yuan decided to notify the United States of the meeting minutes and other documents relating to this incident. I am confident that the Chinese government will be able to take the necessary steps, in accordance with the request of the Executive Yuan, to avoid any actions that could escalate the incident or impede a peaceful resolution. I will immediately consult with the representatives of China and Japan to immediately implement the measures referred to in item 2. I, along with the representatives of Germany, England, France, and Italy, will jointly conduct the aforementioned consultations with the Chinese and Japanese representatives. The measures referred to in item 3 have already been implemented. Spanish Foreign Minister and Chairman of the League of Nations Council, Le Loux. (23rd Special Dispatch)

(Geneva) The telegram from Le Loux, Acting Chairman of the League of Nations Council and Spanish Foreign Minister, to the governments of China and Japan, reads as follows: "Dear Sirs, the League of Nations Council convened a meeting today specifically to discuss the Chinese government's petition regarding the situation in Manchuria, based on Article 11 of the League of Nations Covenant. It is the special directive of the entire body to me, (1) to send an urgent application to the Chinese and Japanese governments to cease any actions that could aggravate the current situation or impede the peaceful resolution of the issue; (2) to confer with the Chinese and Japanese representatives to seek appropriate methods that would allow both countries to immediately withdraw their troops without endangering the safety of their people and industries; (3) the Executive Council has further resolved to forward the records of each meeting and documents concerning the issue to the U.S. government, so that everything is clear. I am deeply confident that your government will be able to respond to the application made by the Executive Council's directive and take all possible steps to prevent any actions that could aggravate the current situation or impede the peaceful resolution of the issue. I will begin consultations with the Chinese and Japanese representatives to implement the second provision. I have obtained the assistance of the representatives of Germany, England, France, and Italy in these discussions. The resolution described in the third provision has now been implemented." Signed by Le Loux. (23rd Reuters Dispatch)

Japanese Aggression

League of Nations Thoroughly Understands 10

Yoshizawa Prevaricates, Claiming He Has Not Received Detailed Reports

Vigorously Obstructs League of Nations Intervention

Envoy Shi Exposes the Truth

British Representative Speaks Righteously

(Geneva) According to news received late tonight, the League of Nations Council, based on its resolution this afternoon, has already telegraphed the governments of China and Japan to halt the expansion of military action in Manchuria. The chief representatives of the United Kingdom, France, Germany, Italy, and other countries in the League of Nations Council held a secret meeting tonight and carefully studied maps of the Far East at the meeting. After the chief representatives of the United Kingdom, France, Germany, and Italy met with Japanese chief representative Yoshizawa, the impression gained by the representatives of various countries was that the actions of the Japanese military in Manchuria were more excessive than the Japanese government was willing to admit.

(Geneva) The League of Nations Council met today to discuss the Manchurian incident. The debate was intense, and adjournments were repeatedly announced to allow the representatives to calm down and talk privately to seek a way to reconcile. However, Japanese representative Yoshizawa vigorously opposed direct intervention by the League of Nations, insisting that instructions from Tokyo had not yet arrived. Therefore, Council President Le Loux announced an adjournment until tomorrow's meeting. No concrete results were obtained today, but slight progress has been made, as Le Loux was commissioned to draft an application to China and Japan, asking them to abide by the letter and spirit of the League of Nations Covenant. This proposal was put forward by British representative Cecil, as detailed information on the dispute has not yet been received, and this is all that the League of Nations can do. Cecil also advocated notifying the United States of all actions of the League of Nations, which was unanimously approved. Le Loux also asked Chinese representative Shi Zhaoji and Japanese representative Yoshizawa to have private talks. Shi agreed, but stated that Japanese troops had invaded and occupied Tongliao County. ⊙Foreign Ministry Lodges Third Emergency Protest with Japan⊙Cai Yuanpei, Zhang Ji, Chen Mingshu, and others went to Guangdong to discuss the unity of Beijing and Guangdong⊙(See Domestic Important Telegrams)Denmark Bans Cash Exports⊙(See Foreign Important Telegrams)Zhang Jia'ao and others telegraphed the United States, asking them to uphold justice in the case of the invasion of the eastern provinces⊙(See Local News)

Page 4

This should not be regarded as direct negotiations between China and Japan, and the Council must continue to discuss the case tomorrow. As the debate proceeded, Yoshizawa vigorously opposed the suggestion that military attachés from the embassies in Beiping and Tokyo go to Manchuria to investigate the origins of the case, saying that the Tokyo government would never agree to this. This case is a matter between China and Japan, and if other countries intervene, it will only aggravate the situation. However, Yoshizawa has temporarily approved the proposal to apply to both governments to stop military action and withdraw troops to their original defenses, but if there are instructions from Tokyo to the contrary, it will still have to be cancelled.

Today, Cecil's proposal was seconded by German representative and Foreign Minister Curtius. Curtius said that applying to China and Japan to stop the escalation of the situation is only a temporary measure, and there should be continued action afterwards. Curtius also said that the League of Nations cannot be afraid to move forward because this issue is thorny. If so, not only will the League of Nations' credibility be swept away, but it will not be able to survive. (22nd National Telegram)

(Geneva) The Japanese army's occupation of South Manchuria is a very serious matter. If it continues to develop, there will be more and more disputes, which will inevitably affect policies outside Manchuria. The League of Nations is now gradually understanding this. Tonight, the League of Nations expressed surprise at the Japanese government's delay in providing detailed reports on the Manchurian incident, as it is known that all transportation in Manchuria is now under the control of the Japanese military authorities. At today's meeting of the League of Nations Executive Council, British representative Cecil strongly urged the Chinese and Japanese troops to immediately retreat to their original locations while the League of Nations studies the case, and said that all countries must avoid incidents like those that occurred in Manchuria. He asked the governments of China and Japan to support the League of Nations' view of aggressive behavior and not to take any further actions that would exacerbate the Manchurian situation. Japanese chief representative Yoshizawa arose and said that he greatly agreed with the noble views expressed by Lord Cecil, and that the Japanese government very much wanted to respect the Briand-Kellogg Pact. Yoshizawa went on to describe Japan's overpopulation and the huge interests that Japan has in Manchuria, and finally said that the Japanese government is very willing to resolve more than 100 county cases that could disturb the friendly relations between China and Japan. Chinese chief representative Shi Zhaoji then arose and reported to the Executive Council the latest news he had received from the Chinese government, and declared that the Chinese military and civilians in Manchuria were abiding by the government's instructions and were being very cautious, not taking actions that could make the situation worse, but the situation in Manchuria is now deteriorating, and he asked the League of Nations Executive Council to order Japan to withdraw its troops in Manchuria to their original locations. What is now before the Executive Council is the issue of the invasion of Chinese territory, which is extremely important and should immediately appoint a commission of inquiry. In short, the Japanese army is still occupying Manchuria, so please order the Japanese army to withdraw immediately. At this point, Le Loux, the Spanish representative and chairman of the Executive Council, moved that the League of Nations issue an urgent telegram to the Chinese and Japanese governments, asking them not to take any actions that could increase the situation in Manchuria or impede the peaceful resolution of this issue. The chairman also proposed a motion stating that the Chinese and Japanese representatives should be consulted to find sufficient methods to enable China and Japan to immediately withdraw their troops without endangering the safety of their nationals or the protection of their industries. The chairman also asked the Executive Council to approve the sending of the minutes of today's meeting and the documents on Manchurian matters to the US government. The Executive Council unanimously expressed its agreement with the above proposals. The Chinese representative said that time is of the essence in resolving the difficulties. The resolution that has just been passed is the first step in the plan that should be adopted. Please conduct an impartial investigation by the League of Nations into the beginning and end of this case. The way to investigate the entire case and establish the compensation that should be given has not yet been blocked, and please reconvene the Executive Council tomorrow. Japanese representative Yoshizawa agreed with the peaceful views expressed by Chinese representative Shi and then said that he would like to notify the Executive Council of all the detailed news about the Manchurian incident, but he could not say for sure that he would receive this news tomorrow. He is now awaiting instructions from the Japanese government regarding its views on this matter. Cecil asked the Japanese representative to promptly urge his government to issue instructions, and said that if the allegation made by Representative Shi that hundreds of men, women and children had been killed in Manchuria was true, then the occurrence of a major incident in Manchuria could be generally seen, so this matter was very important, and the instructions of the Japanese government to its representative in Geneva should be issued promptly. At this point, the discussion ended, and the Chairman of the Executive Council announced that the next meeting to handle this matter would be held at the earliest possible time. The four chief representatives attending the League of Nations this evening, together with the Chinese and Japanese chief representatives, held a closed-door meeting to formulate a text, which was sent to the Chinese and Japanese governments, asking both sides to restrain all actions that could exacerbate the situation. The participants in this meeting were Spanish Chief Representative Le Loux (Spanish Foreign Minister), British Chief Representative Viscount Cecil, German Chief Representative Curtius (German Foreign Minister), Italian Chief Representative Grandi (Italian Foreign Minister), Chinese Chief Representative Shi Zhaoji (Envoy to the United Kingdom), and Japanese Chief Representative Yoshizawa (Japanese Ambassador to France). The results of the discussion have not yet been made public. (22nd Reuters Dispatch)

(Geneva) The League of Nations Council convened a second emergency meeting this afternoon to discuss China's application for intervention in the Manchurian issue and formally resolved to authorize Council President Le Loux to notify China and Japan to prevent the escalation of the situation and order the troops to return to their original defenses. The resolution passed by the entire Council is as follows: (1) Urgently request China and Japan to prevent all actions in Manchuria that could escalate the situation and hinder a peaceful solution; (2) Study with the representatives of China and Japan ways to enable the troops of both countries to withdraw immediately without endangering the lives and property of the people of both countries. The Council also resolved to send all the meeting minutes and all the official documents concerning the Sino-Japanese Manchurian incident to the United States for the reference of the Washington government. Although Chinese representative Shi Zhaoji requested that the meeting be held again on Wednesday, the Council decided to adjourn and wait for President Le Loux to convene it again. President Le Loux, German representative Curtius, French representative Briand, Italian representative Grandi, and representatives of several other countries unanimously maintained that the League of Nations' resolution today was only its first part, and that further actions would be taken until the case was completely resolved. All the representatives on the Council were fearful that the Manchurian issue had reached a critical juncture and that a solution was urgently needed. After the resolution was passed, Envoy Shi expressed his acceptance, but with one understanding, that is, it was recognized that this was only the first step and that more active progress would be made in the future. The various discussions in the future can only be regarded as discussions within the Council and cannot be regarded as direct negotiations between China and Japan. Yoshizawa said that before receiving instructions from Tokyo, he could not provide more information. At this afternoon's meeting, Yoshizawa was nearly persuaded to comply with the Council's meeting procedures, and it took several persuasions before he complied, causing the meeting to be delayed by seventy minutes. The Council heard Yoshizawa's speech in silence and tension this morning. Yoshizawa recounted how Japan respects international treaties, how much Japan has invested in Manchuria, and how Japan is now willing to make every effort to peacefully resolve the Manchurian issue, etc. After Yoshizawa finished speaking, Envoy Shi stood up vigorously and raised a bundle of telegrams, saying, "These are the telegrams I have received since this morning. If you read them, you will know that the situation in Manchuria is deteriorating at any time and that the situation is so urgent that it cannot be delayed any longer. Many good Chinese people have been massacred, and even women and children have not been spared. The issue today is the issue of aggression against China. Our discussion should recognize this statement. The issue is extremely urgent and cannot be delayed. The Chinese people are now shouting themselves hoarse in seeking a peaceful solution." Envoy Shi also said that according to the provisions of the League of Nations Covenant, the Council has an unshirkable duty to resolve the Sino-Japanese dispute. The League of Nations should now send a delegation to Manchuria as soon as possible to investigate the truth. The Japanese troops are occupying more and more Manchurian territory, and the Japanese troops must withdraw from Chinese territory immediately, etc. (22nd National News Agency Telegram)

(Geneva) The League of Nations Secretariat announced today that the Council will convene another special meeting to discuss the Manchurian incident and confirmed that League of Nations President Le Loux sent an urgent telegram to the governments of China and Japan last night, strongly urging both sides to avoid all actions that could escalate the situation and expressing the League of Nations' deep confidence that both sides could withdraw troops invading each other's territory to their original defenses. President Le Loux also formally notified Nanjing and Tokyo that he had begun discussions with the representatives of China and Japan, and that representatives of European powers had also been invited to participate in the discussions. More detailed reports on this incident are now awaited from both sides. (23rd National News Agency Telegram)

Current Affairs Commentary

Japanese Reflection (1) 19

The Japanese Empire, powerfully situated in East Asia, with a global outlook. Its status as a first-class power in the world today is already recognized by the world. This time, it violently invaded our Northeast, with the sounds of troops and horses, displaying a dazzling momentum. Superficially, it further proves the swelling of its national power and the unlimited development of militarism, which is enough to persecute East Asia and shake the world. However, we should not be dazzled by its superficial momentum. If we examine Japan's overall national situation, we can see that Japan itself is full of holes and riddled with crises. This violent act against our Northeast is a reflection of the irreconcilable contradictions within its country. The expansion of the crisis is actually leading it to the end of its road. Alas, Japan! It is too late to save itself, yet it wants to harm others. This is truly strange, and even more pitiful.

What is said here about Japan being surrounded by crises is certainly not due to hostile expectations, nor is it due to speculations based on schadenfreude. It can all be verified by facts.

First, in the midst of the global economic recession, Japan, with its inherent deficiencies, is the first to bear the brunt. The lament of "economic national crisis" is widespread throughout Japan. The concrete manifestation of this phenomenon is the decline of industry and commerce, the reduction of purchasing power, and the excess of imports over exports in international trade. The biggest reason for the decline of industry and commerce is undoubtedly the competition of world tariffs, the shrinkage of the international market, and the fall in the price of silver. However, Japan's weakness in raw materials, the lack of iron and coal, its inability to develop the steel industry, and its competition with European and American countries, stagnating at the stage of light industry, is also a major reason. According to statistics, Japan's iron production in 1927 was 159 in the mainland (unit: thousand), and 423 in Korea. In 1928, it was 158 in the mainland and 443 in Korea. In 1929, it was 150 in the mainland, and there were no statistics for Korea. Its production has been sharply decreasing year by year, which is most obvious. Coal production is also gradually feeling insufficient. According to the report in the "National Situation Illustrated" compiled by Yano Tsuneta in 1931, "......In the future, if our country's iron and steel only aim to be self-sufficient, it will need 8 to 9 million tons of coal. Therefore, in the future, our country will inevitably become a coal-importing country...". The gradual lack of coal and iron means that, on the one hand, the steel industry cannot develop, and on the other hand, the light industry is subject to competition from industrially backward countries and the exclusion of American rayon, which has also plummeted. For example, raw silk, which accounts for 40% of Japan's total exports, had 200,000 bales of inventory last year that could not be sold. The sericulture and silk reeling industries are on the verge of bankruptcy. For example, Japan's cotton exports to Shanghai in March 1930 were 15,963 bales, in April they were 9,727 bales, in March 1931 they were 14,033 bales, and in April they were 7,388 bales. That is, this year's April decreased compared to last year, and April also decreased compared to March. Looking at international trade, the percentage of 1930 compared to 1929 was 34.1%. For example, according to the Japanese Ministry of Finance, since January of this year, the import surplus was 5 million yuan in May, creating a new record of import surplus. From the above-mentioned figures, the decline of light industry can be roughly seen. Not only that, the foundation of modern nation-building depends entirely on steel. If steel relies solely on imports, once imports are cut off, the national foundation will be fundamentally shaken. Therefore, the year-by-year reduction of coal and iron is a major cause of Japan's economic recession in the near term, and a chronic disease of Japan's national destiny in the long term.

The decline of industry and commerce has led to agriculture also falling into a state of panic. The cry of recession resounds throughout the country. The impact has resulted in (1) a sharp decrease in tax revenue, insufficient government revenue, and difficult local finances. According to statistics, this year's budget will be short of 80 million yuan, exceeding the estimated amount of 60 million yuan. It is necessary to tighten austerity measures and reduce salaries. Domestic important telegrams of salary reduction 2

Amidst League of Nations Intervention 20

Japan's Attitude

Insisting on Sino-Japanese Solution Alone

Comments from the London Chronicle

(Tokyo) It is learned from important sources that the Japanese government's declaration on its attitude towards Manchuria has been drafted and is currently under consideration by Foreign Minister Shidehara. It is expected to be released within one or two days. At that time, a copy will be sent to Geneva. The government is now considering the League of Nations' document and expects to respond soon, stating that Japan is willing to withdraw its troops to the railway zone, but first it must negotiate with China (without interference from third parties) regarding guarantees of security and the safety of Japanese lives and property. Japanese newspapers and the public seem to agree with Foreign Minister Shidehara and are willing to reduce the scope of the incident and resolve it as soon as possible. There is absolutely no intention of permanently occupying the currently occupied areas. (Reuters, 23rd)

(Tokyo) The attitude Japan will take towards the League of Nations' request for it to withdraw its troops from Chinese territory in Manchuria is attracting worldwide attention. It is learned that the Japanese government will issue a formal declaration tomorrow, explaining the Tokyo government's position on the Sino-Japanese incident. The declaration has been discussed once by cabinet members. Foreign Minister Shidehara visited Prime Minister Wakatsuki today to discuss the League of Nations' actions. The Foreign Minister told the Prime Minister that it was necessary to issue a statement clarifying Japan's policy, and that it was necessary for Japan to maintain its reputation for fulfilling international obligations and adhering to international faith. Land Minister Minami, Chief of Staff Kanaya, and other military authorities also convened an emergency meeting at the same time. After the meeting, Land Minister Minami told reporters that Japan did not hesitate to withdraw its troops from Manchuria, but hoped that the major powers would understand the Japanese military's actions on Saturday. Land Minister Minami also stated that the Japanese military's actions in Manchuria had not violated the Kellogg-Briand Pact. During the meeting, Japan had not yet received an official telegram from Geneva reporting the League of Nations' actions. According to news telegrams from Geneva, the League of Nations did not understand Japan's attitude of protecting its vested rights in Manchuria. The declaration tomorrow will probably reiterate that the Japanese military's actions in Manchuria since Saturday were in self-defense and that Japan had not provoked a state of war or violated international law. (Kokumin, 23rd)

The London Chronicle published an editorial this morning, giving the motion put forward by the Japanese representative in Geneva that the Sino-Japanese dispute should be resolved by China and Japan themselves a "cold" reception. The newspaper emphasized that the United States and the League of Nations are now closely watching the movement of Japanese troops in the vast land of Manchuria, and other people are also very concerned. For example, Russia is also... The newspaper also said that there is evidence showing that the Japanese commanders have greatly exceeded the limits allowed by the Tokyo government. It is heard that there are very serious differences of opinion in the Tokyo government on this matter. If so, finding a solution may be slightly easier than initially expected. But in any case, the Japanese government must recognize that the path currently being taken is extremely dangerous. Japanese diplomacy has repeatedly demonstrated in a dramatic way its deep understanding of the foolishness of attempting to offend world public opinion. (Reuters, 23rd)

Diplomatic Guarantee of Occupation 21

Result of Dispute Between Japanese Foreign and Land Ministers

Decided on this Novel and Peculiar Term

(Nanjing) The diplomatic community received a telegram from Tokyo stating that the Japanese cabinet held another meeting, during which there was quite a dispute between the Foreign and Land Ministers. The Foreign Minister said that if the army wanted to annex the three northeastern provinces, it would be like swallowing a bomb, which would probably cause international accusations and lead to the same fate as Germany. Therefore, it was decided to have a "diplomatic guarantee of occupation." It was also heard that Land Minister Minami had telegraphed to cancel Doihara's appointment as mayor of Shenyang. (Special dispatch, 23rd)

(Nanjing) Regarding the post-incident measures of the Manchurian Incident, it was initially considered a local issue and it was decided to negotiate with the Northeast authorities. As a result of yesterday's cabinet meeting, it was decided to change the pre-determined policy and negotiate with the Nanjing Central Government. However, Land Minister Minami strongly opposed it at the cabinet meeting, and then decided to obey the government's policy. (Dentsu telegram, 23rd)

(Nanjing) Prime Minister Wakatsuki invited Land Minister Minami to his official residence last night to solicit the Land Minister's opinion on the post-incident measures of the Manchurian Incident. The Land Minister said that according to the current situation, it should not be further expanded, but the people's sentiment on the Chinese side is激越, and there may be some conflicts. The army intends to continue to guarantee the occupation and conduct diplomatic negotiations to resolve the pending issues in Manchuria and Mongolia. Prime Minister Wakatsuki replied that he understood the Land Minister's intentions, but if the propaganda of the military department is too激烈, it may hinder Sino-Japanese negotiations, and hoped that a慎重 attitude would be adopted at this time. Then, they discussed the period of stationing troops and Japan's attitude towards the League of Nations for a long time and reached a consensus. The Prime Minister immediately ordered Secretary-General Kawasaki to visit Foreign Minister Shidehara to report the results of the meeting with the Land Minister. (Dentsu telegram, 23rd)

Foreign Ministry Denies

Proposing Direct Negotiations 24

Contents of Statement by Our Delegation to the League of Nations

(Nanjing) The general idea of the written statement submitted by the Chinese delegation to the Secretary-General of the League of Nations is as follows:

In accordance with the order of the government of this country, please pay attention to the following events, and please convene the Council of the League of Nations immediately in accordance with Article 11 of the Covenant, so as to take the most effective method to ensure international peace. The Chinese delegation notified the Council on the 19th of this month of this serious situation and the fact that China is not responsible for any fault. Since then, it has repeatedly received telegrams from the government of this country, learning that the situation has become more and more serious. The formal troops of Japan have, without cause, begun bombing Chinese troops and Shenyang, while destroying arsenals, barracks, and burning gunpowder depots, and disarming Chinese troops in the Changchun Kuanchengtzu area. Afterwards, they estimated and occupied many important cities in Shenyang and Andong, and public institutions in various places were forcibly occupied, and all transportation institutions were also occupied. In response to this violent behavior, the Chinese army and people, in compliance with the orders of the Chinese government, did not engage in any resistance or other behaviors that could worsen the situation. China, as a member of the League of Nations, believes that the League of Nations should take effective actions in accordance with the provisions of Article 11 of the Covenant with regard to this situation. Therefore, this delegation, in accordance with the order of the Chinese government, requests the Council to take the most effective measures in accordance with the powers granted by Article 11 of the Covenant to prevent the expansion of this situation, so as not to endanger international peace, and to restore the original situation, and to determine the nature and amount of compensation that China should receive for the losses caused by this incident. The Chinese government has decided to abide by the recommendations of the Council and the resolutions of the General Assembly without dissent. (Special dispatch, 23rd)

Japanese Military Forcibly

Disarming Jilin Garrison 29

(Jilin) Negotiations on the peaceful handover of Jilin City by the Japanese army were held by Xi Qia, the chief of staff of the Jilin army, and the commander of the 2nd Duomen Division at the Nagoya Hotel in front of Jilin Station at 9 pm on the 21st. Xi Qia said that the Chinese side was willing to disarm voluntarily and asked not to attack Jilin City. Commander Duomen put forward three conditions: (1) All Chinese military police must be completely disarmed before 5 pm on the 22nd; (2) After the disarmament, the weapons must be taken to the front of Jilin Station, and the ammunition must be taken to the foot of Beishan; (3) If this agreement is violated, the Japanese army will take free action. Xi immediately admitted this and agreed to start disarmament immediately. However, by 5 pm on the 22nd, the Chinese side had only handed over 250 rifles, and most of them had not been handed over. Lieutenant General Duomen plans to hesitate until this afternoon, after which he will resort to force. (Dentsu telegram, 23rd)

(Harbin) All Japanese residents in Jilin have been evacuated. (Special dispatch, 22nd)

National Government

Publishes Proclamation to the People 32

The Government Has Made Its Final Determination

The Whole Country Should Seek Consistent Unity

Organize Your Steps to Listen to the Guidance of the Central Government

Vow to Save the Country and Promote the Spirit of the Nation

(Nanjing) The National Government issued a proclamation to the people on the 23rd. Regarding the attitude that the people of the whole country should take after the atrocities of the Japanese army occurred in the three northeastern provinces, the Central Government has already given detailed instructions. The National Government now summarizes the government's current handling of this incident and the government's hopes for the people, and presents them to the people of the whole country. The seriousness of the nature of the Japanese military's atrocities in the East Province this time is unprecedented. This笙 incident has a great relationship with the survival of our country. When the military atrocities began on the 18th of this month, there was no incident of肇釁 beforehand, and its actions conflicted with international practice and any treaty. It openly invaded our territory, killed our people, and humiliated our military and government officials, and continued the atrocities without end. The humiliation that the Japanese have inflicted on our country is a threat to all civilized countries in the world. The establishment of the League of Nations was originally to prevent war and to seek the collective strength of all countries to prevent aggression. After this incident occurred, the government immediately reported the Japanese atrocities to the League of Nations and requested that the first step be to make the Japanese army withdraw immediately. The禡 League of Nations Administrative Committee has held a meeting and has already made a resolution on withdrawing troops after stopping military action. The government has also telegraphed to the League of Nations Administrative Committee that once the withdrawal is complete, it should immediately find a fair solution to this barbaric incident. It is deeply believed that if this incident is fairly investigated, the League of Nations will be able to give us full justice and reasonable remedy in accordance with its responsibilities. The government has now appealed this case to the Administrative Committee of the League of Nations to await the solution of public reason, so it has strictly ordered the national army to avoid conflict with the Japanese army, and has also uniformly admonished the people to maintain a serious and镇静 attitude. As for the Japanese residents in China, the government has also strictly ordered local officials to protect them carefully. This is the responsibility of a civilized country. We should respond to barbarism with civilization and reveal the crimes of unreasonable atrocities with a reasonable attitude, in order to ensure that justice will prevail. However, in order to maintain the independence of our country, the government has made its final determination and is prepared for self-defense, and will not fail the expectations of the people. At this moment, all domestic disputes should be冰释 immediately. Compatriots across the country should abandon their private opinions, unite together, gather under the National Government, seek security for the country, and seek independence for the nation. Compatriots across the country should especially recognize that there is no way to deal with foreign countries without upholding national unity, and should never allow any意气 or emotion to摇动 the policies and steps determined by the Central Government, so as to affect the determination to save the country consistently. The government is shouldering this difficult task,承危, and is at the critical juncture of存亡绝续. It should only adhere to the Central Government's strategy, pay attention at all times, and make it public to the people of the country at any time. All my compatriots, trust the government, organize your steps, listen to the guidance of the Central Government consistently, vow to save the country, to promote the spirit of our nation, and to redeem our current shame. This is especially what I would like to share with my compatriots across the country. (West telegram, 23rd)

Cancel Hostile Positions 43

(Jinan) Han Fuju recently sent a telegram to Wang Jingwei, Tang Shaocuan, Deng Zeru, Gu Yingfen, and others in Guangdong. The original text is as follows:

Urgent to Mr. Wang Jingwei, Mr. Tang Shaocuan, Mr. Deng Zeru, Mr. Xiao Focheng, Mr. Sun Zhesheng, Mr. Gu Xiangqin, Mr. Chen Bonan, Mr. Li Delin, Mr. Bai Jiansheng, and Mr. Tang Mengxiao in Guangzhou: Greetings. The country is unfortunate, natural and man-made disasters have arisen one after another, this is truly an autumn of crisis and survival, a moment of hairbreadth. I believe that in today's situation, without seeking peace, it is impossible to save the country, and without ending disputes, it is impossible to resist foreign aggression. After years of war in our country, the plight of the people has become unbearable to look back upon, in addition, bandits are everywhere, making it difficult to suppress them, and heaven has sent great disasters, rivers are overflowing, and the lives and property of the people are drifting away with the floods, which cannot be counted. Even if the borders are peaceful and there are no internal wars, and we work together to seek relief, the people's lives and the country's pulse, which are barely surviving, may not easily restore their vitality. Moreover, strong neighbors are pressing on, foreign troubles are already deep, and the loss of China is imminent. In times of crisis and shock, we should unite our efforts, catch up quickly, and save ourselves from danger. The only way to do this is through peace and unification. Gentlemen, you are revolutionary leaders, advanced members of the party and the country, with far-sighted plans and deep considerations, which are admired by the whole country. You have long been familiar with the interests of the country and the nation, and you all adhere to the Prime Minister's doctrine of saving the country and the people. Sharing weal and woe, what hatred and resentment cannot be explained? You will certainly not hold each other down due to differences in political views, causing the great territory of China to be lost. Yesterday, I heard that you gentlemen replied to the three gentlemen Zhang Puquan, et al., that the armies of Guangdong and Guangxi are stationed on the border of Guangdong and Guangxi, and will not lightly start a war. I admire your love of peace, and swords and spears will soon turn into jade and silk. Not only will the displaced compatriots be able to celebrate their recovery, but also the party and the country, which have been painstakingly created, will have a chance of revitalization. However, Fuju cannot stop himself from speaking, because every man is responsible for the rise and fall of the world. When the country is in deep trouble and the people are suffering to the extreme, I cannot remain silent. I dare to sincerely appeal to you gentlemen to immediately cancel the hostile situation and jointly seek survival. One day, the beautiful rivers and mountains will be consolidated, and the descendants of the gods will live forever. When drinking water, remember the source, all thanks to the gifts of you gentlemen. The question of safety, danger, survival, and death depends on this one move. I earnestly express my words, please consider them carefully. Han Fuju kowtows and respectfully submits. (Special dispatch on the 22nd)

London China Association

Discusses Silver Issues 64

Reuters, London, 22nd: The China Association held a meeting today to discuss silver issues. Many people attended. It was decided to organize a silver association, with Huntington as president. Huntington firmly advocates adopting bimetallism to save the world from economic panic. The attendees passed a resolution stating that the restoration of silver's original position in the world's monetary system is the fastest and most effective way to alleviate the sharp drop in prices, and decided to request relevant countries to consult as soon as possible. The attendees also decided to expand the use of silver as currency.

Important News: Rong Zhen's Account

The Truth about the Japanese Army's Atrocities 66

Recounted by Wan Fulin and Others after Arriving in Beijing

Wan Fulin, Bao Wen-yue, Li Shizeng, and Zhang Ji arrived in Beijing at 8:00 AM on the 23rd, traveling by Ford airplane from Ping. They stopped in Xuzhou to refuel and then flew to Beijing, landing at Ming Palace Airport at 2:30 PM. Those who came to welcome them included Shao Lizi and others. They had lunch at the Lizi Society. Reporters wanted to interview Wan, but he declined due to the fatigue of the journey. Bao Wen-yue then received them, showing them the detailed account of Rong Zhen's escape and adding that how to respond to future Japanese atrocities could only be decided after meeting with Chairman Chiang. However, the military and government authorities of the Northeast deeply felt that in the face of foreign aggression, they should resist unanimously. Bao also said that if there were no special matters, he planned to fly back north on the 24th. The full text of Rong Zhen's account is as follows: "The Shenyang incident this time was quite unexpected. At 10:00 PM on the 18th of this month, we heard a loud explosion north of Shenyang, followed by heavy gunfire. Shortly after, we received a report from our 7th Brigade at the North Camp that Japanese soldiers were attacking our barracks. Believing that the Japanese army was provoking trouble without cause, we decided to maintain a calm attitude and ordered our troops not to resist. Before long, the Japanese army broke into the camp, killing and wounding our soldiers. To uphold international trust, our army still adhered to the policy of non-resistance. However, the Japanese army drove and killed soldiers without restraint. Our army had no choice but to withdraw from the barracks, and the Japanese army set fire to them. By 12:00 AM, they were using field guns to bombard our North Camp, the mortar factory, and the arsenal. The arsenal had not sustained major damage until around 5:00 AM. The mortar warehouse was bombed and exploded, and the mortar factory was also occupied. Our officers and soldiers, as well as nearby residents, were unable to escape in time, resulting in many casualties. The exact number has not yet been determined. When the shelling first started, our negotiators immediately questioned the Japanese consul, who claimed that the reason was unknown. We requested that he quickly stop it within five minutes, but the Japanese consul requested another five minutes to handle the stopping procedures. At around 11:00 AM, the Japanese army's shooting continued as before, increasing rather than decreasing, and infantry also attacked the city of Shenyang. We negotiated with the Japanese consul again, but the Japanese consul replied that diplomatic officials could not directly stop military actions. However, the Japanese army continued to advance and did not stop at all. By 8:00 AM on the 19th, they had attacked and entered the city, first climbing the city walls and shooting inside, guarding the four city gates, disarming the military and police, occupying government offices, searching documents, arresting military officers, and searching private residences. All police stations inside and outside the city were attacked by Japanese machine guns. All occupied institutions were marked with signs saying 'Occupied by the Japanese Army; violators will be executed.' Our military and police absolutely did not resist, but a considerable number had already been tragically killed by gunfire. Many of the civilian officials who had not fled were also being monitored and could not move freely. Captured military officers were forced to sign statements admitting that our army had attacked first and destroyed their railway bridges. We took the opportunity to try to negotiate with them, but the Japanese army acted recklessly and disregarded our efforts. Later, we asked consuls from various countries to inquire about the reason for the atrocities, but the Japanese army claimed that the incident was due to our army's destruction of a bridge on the South Manchurian Railway. In fact, the explosive sound at the beginning of the incident was caused by the Japanese army themselves blowing up a small bridge on the South Manchurian Railway near the North Camp. The railway has double tracks, and they only blew up one track. What needs to be clarified? Our army has always tried to avoid conflict with the Japanese army. How could we have destroyed the bridges? They are making something out of nothing and deliberately fabricating lies. At around 9:00 AM, the gunfire had not stopped. The Japanese army claimed that there would be a definitive approach only after Commander Honjo arrived in Shenyang at noon. At 1:00 PM, Honjo indeed arrived in Shenyang and held a military meeting first. After the meeting, we asked if we could negotiate, but they replied that there was no need to negotiate with Chinese military and government officials. If it was for the sake of maintaining local order, representatives elected by the people could negotiate. At 1:00 PM, I went to Chairman Zang's residence to discuss everything. It happened that Japanese soldiers were guarding the back door of the residence, and plainclothes agents were monitoring the front door. I changed my clothes and sneaked out, entering a small household nearby. Afterwards, I moved frequently and changed my clothes. At night, I stayed in a small hotel. On the morning of the 20th, I sneaked into Zang's residence again. While we were talking, Japanese military police actually entered to search. Everyone there urged me to flee. With no other choice, I left Zang's residence and managed to sneak out of the city gate through small alleys. The inspection at the city gate was extremely strict. I was spared only because I had changed my clothes. I detoured to Huanggu Village, boarded a train to Ping. This is the general situation of what happened."

Account from Refugees Fleeing Tianjin

Tragic Situation of Shenyang under Occupation 67

Report from Tianjin: The No. 102 train from Shenyang on the Beining Railway, which departed yesterday (the 19th), arrived in Tianjin at 5:00 PM today (the 20th). According to a passenger, Mr. So-and-so, he went from Tianjin to Shenyang on the 17th and arrived at Nanman Station at 8:00 AM the next morning, staying at the Jiaotong Hotel. He then took a car to visit friends. It rained lightly that day, followed by yellow fog and a black wind, as if foretelling a major disaster. Passing by the governor's office, the guards were unusually deserted. That afternoon, the passenger went to Huanggu Village with a friend for dinner at the Qi's residence. He went to bed slightly drunk. Around midnight, a friend from the transportation sector suddenly knocked on the door and entered, saying that something had happened at the North Camp, that the Japanese army had opened fire, and that the situation had become serious. Upon hearing this shocking news, the passenger was incredibly alarmed. By daybreak (the 19th), he knew that Shenyang had been occupied and boarded the No. 102 train to Shanhaiguan that afternoon. At the time, the train was incredibly crowded, the most ever seen on the Beining Railway. That night, while traveling in a certain location, bandits placed huge stones on the tracks in an attempt to derail the train and rob it. Fortunately, the driver was skilled at using the mechanism and managed to escape danger, but the engine was damaged. It continued to move forward only after repairs. It safely arrived in Tianjin today. The Northeast army retreated and gathered at Dahushan, numbering 30,000 to 40,000 men. He saw vehicles going inland along the way. He also saw 20,000 to 30,000 national troops when the train passed Xinmin Town. He heard that Japanese warships planned to land at Qinhuangdao, but stopped temporarily because ten warships from a certain country were following them.

According to a Mr. So-and-so from a certain agency in the Northeast who came to Tianjin from Liaoning, at dawn on the 19th of this month, the provincial capital of Liaoning heard gunfire. At that time, most people were sound asleep and were awakened from their dreams, thinking that the Japanese were practicing shooting again, not thinking of anything else. Unexpectedly, before long, they poured into the city, with a force of about one division. First, they occupied the North Camp, then they spread to Northeast University. All the students at the university were searched. All transportation facilities in the city, such as telegraph and telephone offices, were occupied. Afterwards, they divided their forces to guard various institutions. As a result, the North Camp and other places were burned down. The fire was most intense at the grain and forage factory and the clothing factory, and all kinds of debris were turned to ashes. Only a part of the arsenal was burned. At that time, the whole city was in a state of chaos. Ordinary citizens fled in a scramble, and many were tragically killed by bayonets. As for the local police and soldiers, because they were ordered not to resist, they were disarmed. The police, because they were responsible for maintaining local security, often directed their fellow citizens who were fleeing in all directions. The Japanese army considered this inappropriate and killed many of them. Statistics show that during the day and night of the 19th, about four to five hundred citizens and eighty to ninety policemen were killed or injured. After this barrage of gunfire, the Japanese army then redistributed their tasks. First, they burned down the Shenyang East Station and dismantled a section of the roadbed, because that road was the hub of the Shenhai intermodal transportation. The purpose was to cut off traffic on both roads. On the one hand, they also sent Japanese soldiers to distribute throughout the city. Whenever they went to a civil or military agency, they forced the people present to hand over all the property and files. Rong Zhen, the chief of the general staff, went to the Japanese consulate to negotiate and ask them to stop military action, but he was detained. At that time, Chairman Zang Shiyi was resting at his private residence, and many Japanese soldiers went to monitor him. It is heard that the Japanese released Rong today, but Chairman Zang is still not free. In addition, the former deputy director of the Beining Railway was also detained once. The residences of various important people were also guarded by the Japanese army, preventing them from entering and leaving. As for the personnel of various institutions, they were allowed to leave or stay as they pleased, but once they left, they were not allowed to enter again. By the afternoon of the 19th, all the institutions had been completely occupied by the Japanese army. In the evening, the order of the city was slightly restored. In addition to collecting firearms, the police were forced to change into civilian clothes and maintain order. The citizens in the city, feeling the obstruction of traffic, could not advance or retreat. Some were indignant and committed suicide. Those who were temporarily safe were also sighing in despair. Therefore, they all scrambled to flee to Huanggu Village, but many were stopped because the San Dong Bridge near Huanggu Village was guarded by the Japanese army, and they were not allowed to pass. Those who wore long gowns were especially obstructed. Those who wore short clothes like laborers could be slightly accommodated, and those who were able to pass, including us, were able to pass because we changed into short clothes. As for the destroyed roads, they were not allowed to be repaired. East-west traffic on the South Manchurian Railway was cut off. Judging from the current situation, the commercial port area in the northwest of Shenyang suffered the greatest loss. In addition to the destruction of most of the public construction, the private losses were even more difficult to calculate. The Shenyang Central Station building and various banks were all sealed off. Residents moved to inland areas in succession. Huanggu Village residents were also short of food, and everyone was eager for people from inland areas to provide relief as soon as possible.

Various circles in the capital.

Anti-Japanese National Salvation Assembly 68

Today, the 23rd, at 9:00 AM, people from all walks of life in the capital held an Anti-Japanese National Salvation Assembly at the public sports field. More than ten thousand people from various sectors, including party, government, military, academia, agriculture, industry, commerce, women, and various popular organizations, participated. The atmosphere was fervent and indignant, with tears flowing freely, unprecedented in past events. The entire venue was filled with an intensely tense anti-Japanese sentiment. The various circumstances are recorded below:

Assembly Venue Situation: Party and national flags were crossed at the main entrance of the assembly venue.

Situation of the Opening of the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Assembly in the Capital

A high-hanging banner read: "Anti-Japanese National Salvation Assembly of All Circles in the Capital." Armed police guards stood on both sides. The entire venue was filled with Boy Scouts maintaining order. After everyone stood in solemn silence, mournful music was played, and ceremonial rites were performed. After the opening speech by Zhou Bomin, Chairman of the Presidium, Lai Lian, Xiang Xueru, Tang Guozhen, Ni Guanghe, Mu Huaxuan, Zheng Luosheng, Zhang Mojun, and others successively gave speeches. Then the discussion of proposals began.

Chairman's Opening Speech: Today, everyone is gathered here for this citizens' assembly in the capital. This is because our eastern neighbor, Japan, has launched troops without cause, occupied our three northeastern provinces, invaded our national territory, and trampled on our national sovereignty. Their tyrannical actions are deeply distressing. Everyone must understand why violent Japan wants to invade China. It is because they are a small country with a small population, while China is vast and rich in resources with a large population. Therefore, Japan hopes to consume its domestic goods in China. In order to survive, violent Japan wants to invade Chinese territory, making it impossible for China to survive. To protect the territory of our ancestors, we must unite as one, to defeat Japanese imperialism. The reason why Japan is coveting and plotting to invade our country is also because of the internal strife in our country and the lack of unity. They saw our weakness and attacked us there. It can be proven that the Chinese people lack united strength. Recalling the past, whenever something happened, in the beginning, everyone was vigorous and passionate, but as time passed and the situation changed, they became indifferent. The current incident in the three northeastern provinces is not comparable to past events. We must permanently imprint in our minds that the enemy is violent Japan. Let us unite and strive for the survival of the Chinese nation in the world and overthrow Japanese imperialism. This is the meaning of today's meeting, and I hope everyone will remember it deeply.

Lai Lian's Speech: Fellow countrymen who are not yet dead, we used to say that Annam, India, Korea, and Burma were subjugated countries. Now, we ourselves are about to become subjugated slaves. Japan has already broken into our Chinese gate. The silent mourning for the compatriots who died in the Northeast just now made people cry sadly. This is because the opportunity for our death has arrived. How are we prepared to die? The only way is to overthrow Japanese imperialism before the country is subjugated. We only ask the central government to declare war on Japan. All the citizens of Nanjing should go to the front line, rush to Japan, and fight to the death. The three northeastern provinces are Chinese territory. Compatriots across the country should unite and be prepared to fight.

Emergency Proposal: Party members Wang Pichen, Luo Ciqi, Kuang Zhuosheng, and fifteen others put forward a very urgent proposal, requesting the central government to order the National Government to immediately dismiss and severely punish Foreign Minister Wang Zhengting, who is selling out the country and flattering Japan, and to clarify the legal punishment. (Explanation) This time, Japan invaded and occupied the eastern provinces, and our army retreated step by step. All responsibility should be borne by Japan. However, when the international community inquired with the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Wang Zhengting replied by telegram, claiming that it was a conflict between Chinese and Japanese troops, reducing Japan's responsibility and increasing China's shame. It seems that this is selling out the country and flattering Japan. There must be other intentions. Now, the Control Yuan has already proposed an impeachment for this matter. If this is not handled, internal traitors will not be eliminated, and how can the country be saved? The public opinion should be expressed to the central government, requesting the National Government to immediately detain Wang Zhengting, dismiss him, and severely punish him, clarifying the legal punishment, in order to punish corrupt officials and apologize to the Party and the country. We also implore the gentlemen of the Presidium not to suppress this case in order to protect Wang Zhengting's treasonous behavior, which would be abandoned by the people of the whole country.

Organized Parade: After the proposal was passed, Commander-in-Chief Zhang Qiqing reported on the organization of the parade and demonstration, and a petition to the National Government. Parade route: (1) Party departments at all levels, (2) Administrative organs, (3) Public organizations, (4) Schools, (5) Free public organizations, (6) Military police. The route starts from the assembly venue, passes through Dazhong Bridge, Huaiqing Bridge, Yaojia Lane, Confucius Temple, Sixiang Bridge, Taiping Road, Yanggong Well, Erlang Temple, Beting Lane, to the National Government for a petition, and then disperses at Zhongshan Road. Along the way, Party Boy Scouts will serve as disciplinarians and shout slogans, which is extremely passionate.

Assembly Proposals: (1) Send a telegram to the whole country, urging everyone to unite, swear to resist Japan to the death, and jointly save the country from disaster. (2) Send a telegram to national party and government leaders, urging them to quell internal disputes, unite as one, and jointly resist violent Japan. (3) Send a telegram to compatriots across the country, urging them to jointly organize national salvation volunteer teams and strongly support the government. (4) Send a telegram to compatriots across the country, urging them to endure hardship and persevere, and to have permanent economic severance with Japan. (5) Petition the central government to issue an order to the whole country to dismiss all Japanese people employed by party and government agencies. (6) Send a telegram to the people of all provinces, cities, and counties to unite and organize anti-Japanese national salvation associations, and establish a national general office in the capital. (7) Urge the leaders in Guangdong to cease disputes immediately, concentrate in the capital, and jointly face the national crisis. (8) Petition the central government and the National Government to urge Mr. Hu Hanmin to resume his duties after his leave, and the entire presidium of this assembly will go to Mr. Hu's residence to urge him. (9) Send a telegram to all countries in the world, announcing Japan's atrocities, and request them to uphold justice and maintain world peace. (10) Send a telegram to compatriots across the country, urging them not to hire Japanese people and not to be hired by Japanese people. (11) Request the central government to order the National Government to immediately dismiss and severely punish Foreign Minister Wang Zhengting, who is selling out the country and flattering Japan, and to clarify the legal punishment, in order to punish him for abusing the international telegram, saying that the affairs of the eastern provinces are conflicts between Chinese and Japanese troops, reducing Japan's responsibility and increasing China's shame. (12) Send a telegram to the whole country to stop entertainment. (13) Petition the central government to restore the people's movement to boost morale. (14) Request the government to order the whole country to arm all citizens from tomorrow onwards. (15) Go to the National Government to petition for a declaration of war on Japan. Everyone present at the meeting today is willing to be a volunteer army. (16) Send a telegram to overseas Chinese and compatriots across the country to raise national salvation funds. (17) Organize the Chinese National Salvation Assembly. (18) Request the central government to issue a national mobilization order as soon as possible, and urge Commander-in-Chief Chiang to concentrate military strength and declare war on Japan in order to maintain national integrity.

Executive Yuan

Fortieth National Affairs Meeting 70

Methods for Flood Relief Submitted to Departments for Review

Yan Huiqing Appointed as Minister to the United States

On the 22nd, the Executive Yuan held its fortieth National Affairs Meeting. Song Ziwen, Wang Zhengting, Li Shuhua, Kong Xiangxi, Wang Boqun, Ma Fuxiang, and Liu Ruiheng attended. Chen Shaokuan, Deputy Minister of Naval Affairs, Chen Yi, Deputy Minister of Military Affairs, Lu Bichou, Secretary-General, and Xu Jingzhi, Director of Political Affairs, were present. Song Ziwen chaired the meeting. The matters discussed are as follows: (1) The proposal of the President of the Yuan, Chiang, stated that the current floods along the Yangtze River are unprecedented. In addition to fundamental dredging, the competent authorities should make comprehensive plans. As an immediate solution, the provincial governments should be instructed to thoroughly investigate the area and boundaries of the major lakes in their jurisdiction in the past, as well as the amount of encroachment by polders over time. The previous major floods broke through various polders. If they were newly built in the past sixty years since Minister to the United States Yan Huiqing

arrived and were indeed within the old lakebed, they should not be repaired again in order to return the fields to the lakes, restore their original state, and allow the rivers to have adequate storage space. The number of abandoned fields should be investigated, and future land taxes should be exempted. It is strictly forbidden to compete with the water for profit. Furthermore, water management cannot be effective without comprehensive planning for the Yellow River, Huai River, and Yangtze River. In the past, the various schemes for guiding the Huai River had proposals for draining the fields of Gaoyou, Baoying, and Shaobo Lakes, as well as disputes over diverting water into the sea or the river. Because the project of diverting water into the sea is larger, those who support diverting water into the river are in the majority. Based on the observation of this flood, greater flexibility should be added. While maintaining the original state of the lakes, although we still advocate both diverting water into the river and dredging the sea, we should start with diverting water into the sea first to ensure complete safety and avoid future troubles. The above two points are to be submitted to the competent authorities and the relevant provincial governments for consideration and handling. If there are concrete plans that should be stipulated, they should be drafted and submitted for approval and implementation. Is this appropriate? Please make a public decision. Resolution: Submit to the Ministers of Interior, Industry, and Transportation to convene experts and relevant agencies to review the matter jointly. (2) The Ministry of Foreign Affairs submitted the regulations of the National Sacrifice Problem Research Committee. Please review and submit for record. Resolution: Passed and submitted for record. (3) The Ministry of Military Affairs submitted the draft regulations for awarding commemorative medals for suppressing the Reds in the Army, Navy, and Air Force, as well as the design of the commemorative medal; the draft regulations for issuing certificates to local militias; and the preferential treatment measures for members of the Jiangxi, Fujian, Hunan, and Hubei militias who died in action while suppressing the Reds, and their families. Please review and submit for promulgation and implementation. Resolution: Submit to the Ministry of Interior for review. (4) Resolution: Wu Nanxuan, President of National Tsinghua University, submitted his resignation. Please approve it and appoint Mei Yiqi to succeed him. Before he arrives at the school, Weng Wenhao will continue to act as president. (5) Resolution: Wu Chaoshu, Minister to the United States, requested to resign. Please approve it and appoint Yan Huiqing to fill the vacancy.

Local Communications

Wuxi 71

Telegram Requesting Severe Censure of Northeast Authorities: Qian Sunqing, chairman of the Wuxi County Chamber of Commerce, telegraphed the central government regarding the Northeast war, requesting severe censure of the responsible authorities in the Northeast to appease the nation. The telegram stated: "In this Northeast incident, the Japanese attributed it to local issues. However, the local authorities failed to fulfill their responsibility to defend the territory, and their fault is undeniable. They were negligent in their defense beforehand, and fled in panic when the incident occurred. They usually boasted of having troops to defend themselves, but not a single arrow was fired. National territory was handed over to the enemy with both hands, and countless people were killed and injured. Officials were humiliated and endured humiliation in order to survive. The enemy penetrated deep into our territory, and our territory shrank by hundreds of miles every day, while the commander-in-chief leisurely stayed in the old capital, almost forgetting what his position was. He lacked the fear of the three armies. Losing the army and disgracing the country is unprecedented. If there is any conscience left, they should commit suicide to show their determination. Otherwise, the national law should be strictly enforced to impeach them, so as to appease the nation. International relief should also be sought to protect the territory. Otherwise, the country will perish soon, and what diplomacy can be discussed? The central government should strictly order them by telegram to make meritorious deeds and serve the country. The lost territory should be recovered quickly, and the territory that has not been lost should be protected properly. Any retreat will be severely punished. This will boost morale and make amends for the lost sheep. We express our words with tears and trepidation."

County Police Team Repeatedly Captures Notorious Bandits: A notorious bandit who roams between Suzhou and Changzhou, nicknamed "Old Granny," has committed many crimes in the Changzhou area. She is good at disguise and particularly cunning. She can hold a gun with both hands, walk hunched over, and fire quickly to the left and right, hitting the target every time. Although the authorities have sent out many scouts, it is still difficult to capture her. Recently, due to a gang robbery case at the home of a certain family in Qishuyan, the police team has been strictly ordered to arrest her. She fled to Wuxi. The detectives You Quangen and Chen Shouwen of the Wujin Public Security Bureau, along with an informant, came to Wuxi to assist the Wuxi detectives in searching everywhere. They were captured in the No. 1 theater on Guangqin Road and taken to the Public Security Bureau for interrogation. They were then escorted back to Changzhou for further investigation. Furthermore, according to a tip-off, the main suspect, Li Fuan, who robbed a policeman of his gun outside the South Gate last year, recently sneaked into Wuxi again. Chief Liao led the detectives to investigate and arrested him at the back door of the Qitai Inn in Changkangli. A wooden toy gun was found on him. The suspect was wearing a blue cloth gown and a felt hat. He was from Shouxian, Anhui. He confessed that he committed a crime at the Fifteen Hole Bridge in Changzhou on the 12th of this month and was pursued by the local security team. His wife, Li Xue, and four accomplices were captured. He fled to Wuxi. He also confessed that after robbing the gun in Wuxi last year, he went to Yichong to serve as a police officer. He fled shortly afterwards. He also has a boat, which was also seized in Changzhou.

Telegram Requesting Dismissal and Punishment of County Magistrate Who Suppresses Public Sentiment: After Wuxi Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association received news of the Japanese troops attacking the eastern provinces, County Magistrate Chen Chuande immediately sent people to various newspapers to prevent the publication of anti-Japanese news. He also prevented people from participating in anti-Japanese work, pretending to be calm and suppressing public sentiment. The County Supervisory Committee has already decided to issue a warning. When all circles held a mass rally, more than 100,000 people participated, but not a single member of the county government attended and secretly obstructed it. They only know how to be officials and do not know how to love the country. Yesterday, a telegram was sent to the Provincial Party Department and the Provincial Government, requesting immediate dismissal and severe punishment to appease the public.

Changzhou 72

Emergency Meeting of the Chamber of Commerce to Resist Japan: At 5:00 PM on the 22nd, the Wuyi County Chamber of Commerce convened leaders from various industries to hold an emergency meeting to resist Japan. The matters discussed were: (1) The violent Japanese forcefully occupied the eastern provinces, and our country is on the verge of extinction. How should we deal with this? The meeting decided (A) to send a telegram advocating a united declaration of war on Japan, (B) to send a telegram urging the comrades in Guangdong to cease the war and make peace, (C) to comply with the order to notify all merchants and markets to lower the flag to half-mast for one day on the 23rd to express mourning, (D) to suspend business for half a day in the entire city on the morning of the 24th to express indignation, (E) to have all industries participate in the anti-Japanese national salvation mass rally, and (F) to intensify anti-Japanese work. (2) To inform the merchants' committee on economic severance with Japan to intensify their work.
